<DIV id="page_55">


<DIV id="id_1">
<DIV id="id_1_1">
<P class="p122 ft1">Konventionen om klusterammunition</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_1_2">
<P class="p122 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</P>
<P class="p183 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p218 ft37">DIPLOMATIC CONFERENCE FOR THE ADOPTION OF A CONVENTION ON CLUSTER MUNITIONS</P>
<P class="p219 ft18">DUBLIN 19 – 30 MAY 2008</P>
<P class="p220 ft18">Convention on Clustermunitions</P>
<P class="p221 ft16"><SPAN class="ft15">Deeply concerned </SPAN>that civilian populations and individual civilians continue to bear the brunt of armed conflict,</P>
<P class="p222 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">Determined </SPAN>to put an end for all time to the suffering and casualties caused by cluster munitions at the time of their use, when they fail to function as intended or when they are abandoned,</P>
<P class="p223 ft2"><SPAN class="ft3">Concerned </SPAN>that cluster munition remnants kill or maim civilians, including women and children, obstruct economic and social development, including through the loss of livelihood, impede postconflict rehabilitation and reconstruction, delay or prevent the return of refugees and internally displaced persons, can negatively impact on national and international <NOBR>peace-building</NOBR> and humanitarian assistance efforts, and have other severe consequences that can persist for many years after use,</P>
<P class="p224 ft16"><SPAN class="ft15">Deeply concerned </SPAN>also at the dangers presented by the large national stockpiles of cluster munitions retained for operational use and <SPAN class="ft15">determined </SPAN>to ensure their rapid destruction,</P>
<P class="p225 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">Believing </SPAN>it necessary to contribute effectively in an efficient, coordinated manner to resolving the challenge of removing cluster munition remnants located throughout the world, and to ensure their destruction,</P>
<P class="p222 ft16"><SPAN class="ft15">Determined </SPAN>also to ensure the full realisation of the rights of all cluster munition victims and <SPAN class="ft15">recognising </SPAN>their inherent dignity,</P>
<P class="p222 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">Resolved </SPAN>to do their utmost in providing assistance to cluster munition victims, including medical care, rehabilitation and psychological support, as well as providing for their social and economic inclusion,</P>
<P class="p226 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">Recognising </SPAN>the need to provide ageand <NOBR>gender-sensitive</NOBR> assistance to cluster munition victims and to address the special needs of vulnerable groups,</P>
<P class="p223 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">Bearing in mind </SPAN>the Convention on the Rights of Persons with Disabilities which, <SPAN class="ft20">inter alia</SPAN>, requires that States Parties to that Convention undertake to ensure and promote the full realisation of all</P>
<P class="p227 ft2">55</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_56">


<DIV>
<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p19 ft16">human rights and fundamental freedoms of all persons with disabilities without discrimination of any kind on the basis of disability,</P>
<P class="p228 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">Mindful </SPAN>of the need to coordinate adequately efforts undertaken in various fora to address the rights and needs of victims of various types of weapons, and <SPAN class="ft20">resolved </SPAN>to avoid discrimination among victims of various types of weapons,</P>
<P class="p229 ft2"><SPAN class="ft3">Reaffirming </SPAN>that in cases not covered by this Convention or by other international agreements, civilians and combatants remain under the protection and authority of the principles of international law, derived from established custom, from the principles of humanity and from the dictates of public conscience,</P>
<P class="p230 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">Resolved </SPAN>also that armed groups distinct from the armed forces of a State shall not, under any circumstances, be permitted to engage in any activity prohibited to a State Party to this Convention,</P>
<P class="p229 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">Welcoming </SPAN>the very broad international support for the international norm prohibiting <NOBR>anti-personnel</NOBR> mines, enshrined in the 1997 Convention on the Prohibition of the Use, Stockpiling, Production and Transfer of <NOBR>Anti-Personnel</NOBR> Mines and on Their Destruction,</P>
<P class="p229 ft2"><SPAN class="ft3">Welcoming </SPAN>also the adoption of the Protocol on Explosive Remnants of War, annexed to the Convention on Prohibitions or Restrictions on the Use of Certain Conventional Weapons Which May be Deemed to be Excessively Injurious or to Have Indiscriminate Effects, and its entry into force on 12 November 2006, and wishing to enhance the protection of civilians from the effects of cluster munition remnants in <NOBR>post-conflict</NOBR> environments,</P>
<P class="p230 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">Bearing in mind </SPAN>also United Nations Security Council Resolution 1325 on women, peace and security and United Nations Security Council Resolution 1612 on children in armed conflict,</P>
<P class="p229 ft16"><SPAN class="ft15">Welcoming </SPAN>further the steps taken nationally, regionally and globally in recent years aimed at prohibiting, restricting or suspending the use, stockpiling, production and transfer of cluster munitions,</P>
<P class="p231 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">Stressing </SPAN>the role of public conscience in furthering the principles of humanity as evidenced by the global call for an end to civilian suffering caused by clustermunitions and <SPAN class="ft20">recognising </SPAN>the efforts to that end undertaken by the United Nations, the International Committee of the Red Cross, the Cluster Munition Coalition and numerous other nongovernmental organisations around the world,</P>
<P class="p231 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">Reaffirming </SPAN>the Declaration of the Oslo Conference on Cluster Munitions, by which, inter alia, States recognised the grave consequences caused by the use of cluster munitions and committed themselves to conclude by 2008 a legally binding instrument that would prohibit the use, production, transfer and stockpiling of cluster munitions</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p111 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</P>
<P class="p232 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p233 ft2">56</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_57">


<P class="p234 ft4">that cause unacceptable harm to civilians, and would establish a Prop. 2011/12:47 framework for cooperation and assistance that ensures adequate Bilaga 1 provision of care and rehabilitation for victims, clearance of</P>
<P class="p218 ft16">contaminated areas, risk reduction education and destruction of stockpiles,</P>
<P class="p235 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">Emphasising </SPAN>the desirability of attracting the adherence of all States to this Convention, and <SPAN class="ft20">determined </SPAN>to work strenuously towards the promotion of its universalisation and its full implementation,</P>
<P class="p223 ft2"><SPAN class="ft3">Basing </SPAN>themselves on the principles and rules of international humanitarian law, in particular the principle that the right of parties to an armed conflict to choose methods or means of warfare is not unlimited, and the rules that the parties to a conflict shall at all times distinguish between the civilian population and combatants and between civilian objects and military objectives and accordingly direct their operations against military objectives only, that in the conduct of military operations constant care shall be taken to spare the civilian population, civilians and civilian objects and that the civilian population and individual civilians enjoy general protection against dangers arising from military operations,</P>
<P class="p3 ft18">HAVE AGREED <SPAN class="ft2">as follows:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p236 ft2">Article 1</P>
<P class="p237 ft3">General obligations and scope of application</P>
<P class="p238 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft45">Each State Party undertakes never under any circumstances to:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p239 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Use cluster munitions;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p240 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">Develop, produce, otherwise acquire, stockpile, retain or transfer to anyone, directly or indirectly, cluster munitions;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p240 ft16"><SPAN class="ft2">(c)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft48">Assist, encourage or induce anyone to engage in any activity prohibited to a State Party under this Convention.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p225 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Paragraph 1 of this Article applies, mutatis mutandis, to explosive bomblets that are specifically designed to be dispersed or released from dispensers affixed to aircraft.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p241 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">3.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft45">This Convention does not apply to mines.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p236 ft2">Article 2</P>
<P class="p242 ft3">Definitions</P>
<P class="p243 ft2">For the purposes of this Convention:</P>
<P class="p244 ft2">1. “<SPAN class="ft18">Cluster munition victims</SPAN>” means all persons who have been killed or suffered physical or psychological injury, economic loss, social marginalisation or substantial impairment of the realisation of their rights caused by the use of cluster munitions. They include those persons directly impacted by cluster munitions as well as their affected families and communities;</P>
<P class="p99 ft2">57</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_58">


<P class="p19 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft45">“</SPAN><SPAN class="ft18">Cluster munition</SPAN>” means a conventional munition that is Prop. 2011/12:47</P>
<P class="p245 ft4">designed to disperse or release explosive submunitions each weighing Bilaga 1 less than 20 kilograms, and includes those explosive submunitions. It</P>
<P class="p122 ft2">does not mean the following:</P>
<P class="p246 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">A munition or submunition designed to dispense flares, smoke, pyrotechnics or chaff; or a munition designed exclusively for an air defence role;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p246 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">A munition or submunition designed to produce electrical or electronic effects;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p246 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(c)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">A munition that, in order to avoid indiscriminate area effects and the risks posed by unexploded submunitions, has all of the following characteristics:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p247 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(i)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft50">Each munition contains fewer than ten explosive submunitions;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p247 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(ii)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft51">Each explosive submunition weighs more than four kilograms;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p247 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(iii)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft52">Each explosive submunition is designed to detect and engage a single target object;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p247 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(iv)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft53">Each explosive submunition is equipped with an electronic selfdestruction mechanism;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p247 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(v)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft50">Each explosive submunition is equipped with an electronic selfdeactivating feature;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p248 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">3.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft54">“</SPAN><SPAN class="ft19">Explosive submunition</SPAN>” means a conventional munition that in order to perform its task is dispersed or released by a cluster munition and is designed to function by detonating an explosive charge prior to, on or after impact;</P>
<P class="p249 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">4.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft54">“</SPAN><SPAN class="ft19">Failed cluster munition</SPAN>” means a cluster munition that has been fired, dropped, launched, projected or otherwise delivered and which should have dispersed or released its explosive submunitions but failed to do so;</P>
<P class="p248 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">5.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">“</SPAN><SPAN class="ft19">Unexploded submunition</SPAN>” means an explosive submunition that has been dispersed or released by, or otherwise separated from, a cluster munition and has failed to explode as intended;</P>
<P class="p248 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">6.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">“</SPAN><SPAN class="ft19">Abandoned cluster munitions</SPAN>” means cluster munitions or explosive submunitions that have not been used and that have been left behind or dumped, and that are no longer under the control of the party that left them behind or dumped them. They may or may not have been prepared for use;</P>
<P class="p249 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">7.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">“</SPAN><SPAN class="ft19">Cluster munition remnants</SPAN>” means failed cluster munitions, abandoned cluster munitions, unexploded submunitions and unexploded bomblets;</P>
<P class="p248 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">8.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">“</SPAN><SPAN class="ft19">Transfer</SPAN>” involves, in addition to the physical movement of cluster munitions into or from national territory, the transfer of title to</P>
<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t21">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr19 td51"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">and control over cluster munitions, but does not involve the transfer of</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr19 td44"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr21 td51"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">territory containing cluster munition remnants;</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr21 td44"><SPAN class="p15 ft2">58</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_59">


<P class="p250 ft4">Prop. 2011/12:47 9. <NOBR>“<SPAN class="ft19">Self-destruction</SPAN></NOBR><SPAN class="ft19"> mechanism</SPAN>” means an incorporated Bilaga 1 automaticallyfunctioning mechanism which is in addition to the primary</P>
<P class="p251 ft16">initiating mechanism of the munition and which secures the destruction of the munition into which it is incorporated;</P>
<P class="p252 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">10.</SPAN><NOBR><SPAN class="ft55">“</SPAN><SPAN class="ft19">Self-deactivating</SPAN>”</NOBR> means automatically rendering a munition inoperable by means of the irreversible exhaustion of a component, for example a battery, that is essential to the operation of the munition;</P>
<P class="p253 ft37"><SPAN class="ft2">11.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft56">“</SPAN>Cluster munition contaminated area<SPAN class="ft16">” means an area known or suspected to contain cluster munition remnants;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p254 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">12.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft55">“</SPAN><SPAN class="ft19">Mine</SPAN>” means a munition designed to be placed under, on or near the ground or other surface area and to be exploded by the presence, proximity or contact of a person or a vehicle;</P>
<P class="p255 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">13.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft55">“</SPAN><SPAN class="ft19">Explosive bomblet</SPAN>” means a conventional munition, weighing less than 20 kilograms, which is not <NOBR>self-propelled</NOBR> and which, in order to perform its task, is dispersed or released by a dispenser, and is designed to function by detonating an explosive charge prior to, on or after impact;</P>
<P class="p254 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">14.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft55">“</SPAN><SPAN class="ft19">Dispenser</SPAN>” means a container that is designed to disperse or release explosive bomblets and which is affixed to an aircraft at the time of dispersal or release;</P>
<P class="p255 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">15.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft55">“</SPAN><SPAN class="ft19">Unexploded bomblet</SPAN>” means an explosive bomblet that has been dispersed, released or otherwise separated from a dispenser and has failed to explode as intended.</P>
<P class="p256 ft2">Article 3</P>
<P class="p257 ft3">Storage and stockpile destruction</P>
<P class="p258 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Each State Party shall, in accordance with national regulations, separate all cluster munitions under its jurisdiction and control from munitions retained for operational use and mark them for the purpose of destruction.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p253 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Each State Party undertakes to destroy or ensure the destruction of all cluster munitions referred to in paragraph 1 of this Article as soon as possible but not later than eight years after the entry into force of this Convention for that State Party. Each State Party undertakes to ensure that destruction methods comply with applicable international standards for protecting public health and the environment.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p252 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">3.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">If a State Party believes that it will be unable to destroy or ensure the destruction of all cluster munitions referred to in paragraph 1 of this Article within eight years of entry into force of this Convention for that State Party it may submit a request to a Meeting of States Parties or a Review Conference for an extension of the deadline for completing the</SPAN></P>
<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t22">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr16 td51"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">destruction of such cluster munitions by a period of up to four years. A</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr16 td44"><SPAN class="p15 ft2">59</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_60">


<P class="p259 ft4">State Party may, in exceptional circumstances, request additional Prop. 2011/12:47 extensions of up to four years. The requested extensions shall not exceed Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p260 ft16">the number of years strictly necessary for that State Party to complete its obligations under paragraph 2 of this Article.</P>
<P class="p261 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">4.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">Each request for an extension shall set out:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p262 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The duration of the proposed extension;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">A detailed explanation of the proposed extension, including the financial and technical means available to or required by the State Party for the destruction of all cluster munitions referred to in paragraph 1 of this Article and, where applicable, the exceptional circumstances justifying it;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p264 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(c)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">A plan for how and when stockpile destruction will be completed;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(d)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The quantity and type of cluster munitions and explosive submunitions held at the entry into force of this Convention for that State Party and any additional cluster munitions or explosive submunitions discovered after such entry into force;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p264 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(e)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">The quantity and type of cluster munitions and explosive submunitions destroyed during the period referred to in paragraph 2 of this Article; and</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(f)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft58">The quantity and type of cluster munitions and explosive submunitions remaining to be destroyed during the proposed extension and the annual destruction rate expected to be achieved.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p265 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">5.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">The Meeting of States Parties or the Review Conference shall, taking into consideration the factors referred to in paragraph 4 of this Article, assess the request</SPAN></P>
<P class="p266 ft4">and decide by a majority of votes of States Parties present and voting whether to grant the request for an extension. The States Parties may decide to grant a shorter extension than that requested and may propose benchmarks for the extension, as appropriate. A request for an extension shall be submitted a minimum of nine months prior to the Meeting of States Parties or the Review Conference at which it is to be considered.</P>
<P class="p267 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">6.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">Notwithstanding the provisions of Article 1 of this Convention, the retention or acquisition of a limited number of cluster munitions and explosive submunitions for the development of and training in cluster munition and explosive submunition detection, clearance or destruction techniques, or for the development of cluster munition </SPAN><NOBR>counter-measures,</NOBR> is permitted. The amount of explosive submunitions retained or acquired shall not exceed the minimum number absolutely necessary for these purposes.</P>
<P class="p268 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">7.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Notwithstanding the provisions of Article 1 of this Convention, the transfer of cluster munitions to another State Party for the purpose of destruction, as well as for the purposes described in paragraph 6 of this Article, is permitted.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p127 ft2">60</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_61">


<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t23">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr12 td23"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">8.</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr12 td52"><SPAN class="p269 ft2">States Parties retaining, acquiring or transferring cluster munitions</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr12 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD colspan=2 class="tr19 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">orexplosive submunitions for the purposes described in paragraphs 6 and</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr19 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Bilaga 1</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P class="p206 ft2">7 of this Article shall submit a detailed report on the planned and actual use of these cluster munitions and explosive submunitions and their type, quantity and lot numbers. If cluster munitions or explosive submunitions are transferred to another State Party for these purposes, the report shall include reference to the receiving party. Such a report shall be prepared for each year during which a State Party retained, acquired or transferred cluster munitions or explosive submunitions and shall be submitted to the <NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations no later than 30 April of the following year.</P>
<P class="p270 ft2">Article 4</P>
<P class="p271 ft15">Clearance and destruction of cluster munition remnants and risk reduction education</P>
<P class="p254 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Each State Party undertakes to clear and destroy, or ensure the clearance and destruction of, cluster munition remnants located in cluster munition contaminated areas under its jurisdiction or control, as follows:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p272 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Where cluster munition remnants are located in areas under its jurisdiction or control at the date of entry into force of this Convention for that State Party, such clearance and destruction shall be completed as soon as possible but not later than ten years from that date;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p272 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Where, after entry into force of this Convention for that State Party, cluster munitions have become cluster munition remnants located in areas under its jurisdiction or control, such clearance and destruction must be completed as soon as possible but not later than ten years after the end of the active hostilities during which such cluster munitions became cluster munition remnants; and</SPAN></P>
<P class="p273 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(c)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">Upon fulfilling either of its obligations set out in subparagraphs (a) and (b) of this paragraph, that State Party shall make a declaration of compliance to the next Meeting of States Parties.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p253 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">In fulfilling its obligations under paragraph 1 of this Article, each State Party shall take the following measures as soon as possible, taking into consideration the provisions of Article 6 of this Convention regarding international cooperation and assistance:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p272 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">Survey, assess and record the threat posed by cluster munition remnants, making every effort to identify all cluster munition contaminated areas under its jurisdiction or control;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p274 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Assess and prioritise needs in terms of marking, protection of civilians, clearance and destruction, and take steps to mobilise resources and develop a national plan to carry out these activities, building, where appropriate, upon existing structures, experiences and methodologies;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p275 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(c)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Take all feasible steps to ensure that all cluster munition</SPAN></P>
<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t24">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr16 td34"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">contaminated areas under its jurisdiction or control are</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr16 td44"><SPAN class="p15 ft2">61</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_62">


<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t25">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr12 td55"><SPAN class="p14 ft2"><NOBR>perimeter-marked,</NOBR> monitored and protected by fencing or</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr12 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr19 td55"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">other means to ensure the effective exclusion of civilians.</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr19 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Bilaga 1</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr20 td55"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Warning signs based on methods of marking readily</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr20 td55"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">recognisable by the affected community should be utilised in</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr19 td55"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">the marking of suspected hazardous areas. Signs and other</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr19 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr20 td55"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">hazardous area boundary markers should, as far as possible,</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr20 td55"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">be visible, legible, durable and resistant to environmental</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr19 td55"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">effects and should clearly identify which side of the marked</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr19 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr20 td55"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">boundary is considered to be within the cluster munition</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr19 td55"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">contaminated areas and which side is considered to be safe;</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr19 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P class="p246 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(d)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Clear and destroy all cluster munition remnants located in areas under its jurisdiction or control; and</SPAN></P>
<P class="p246 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(e)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">Conduct risk reduction education to ensure awareness among civilians living in or around cluster munition contaminated areas of the risks posed by such remnants.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p249 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">3.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">In conducting the activities referred to in paragraph 2 of this Article, each State Party shall take into account international standards, including the International Mine Action Standards (IMAS).</SPAN></P>
<P class="p248 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">4.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">This paragraph shall apply in cases in which cluster munitions have been used or abandoned by one State Party prior to entry into force of this Convention for that State Party and have become cluster munition remnants that are located in areas under the jurisdiction or control of another State Party at the time of entry into force of this Convention for the latter.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p276 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">In such cases, upon entry into force of this Convention for both States Parties, the former State Party is strongly encouraged to provide, inter alia, technical, financial, material or human resources assistance to the latter State Party, either bilaterally or through a mutually agreed third party, including through the United Nations system or other relevant organisations, to facilitate the marking, clearance and destruction of such cluster munition remnants.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p277 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">Such assistance shall include, where available, information on types and quantities of the cluster munitions used, precise locations of cluster munition strikes and areas in which cluster munition remnants are known to be located.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p248 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">5.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">If a State Party believes that it will be unable to clear and destroy or ensure the clearance and destruction of all cluster munition remnants referred to in paragraph 1 of this Article within ten years of the entry into force of this Convention for that State Party, it may submit a request to a Meeting of States Parties or a Review Conference for an extension of the deadline for completing the clearance and destruction of such cluster munition remnants by a period of up to five years. The requested extension shall not exceed the number of years strictly necessary for that State Party to complete its obligations under paragraph 1 of this Article.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p230 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">6.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">A request for an extension shall be submitted to a Meeting of</SPAN></P>
<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t26">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr16 td51"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">States Parties or a Review Conference prior to the expiry of the time</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr16 td44"><SPAN class="p15 ft2">62</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_63">


<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t27">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr12 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">period referred to in paragraph 1 of this Article for that State Party. Each</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr12 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr19 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">request shall be submitted a minimum of nine months prior to the</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr19 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Bilaga 1</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr20 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Meeting of States Parties or Review Conference at which it is to be</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr19 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">considered. Each request shall set out:</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr19 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P class="p239 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The duration of the proposed extension;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p240 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft59">A detailed explanation of the reasons for the proposed extension, including the financial and technical means available to and required by the State Party for the clearance and destruction of all cluster munition remnants during the proposed extension;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p240 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(c)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The preparation of future work and the status of work already conducted under national clearance and demining programmes during the initial ten year period referred to in paragraph 1 of this Article and any subsequent extensions;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p278 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(d)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The total area containing cluster munition remnants at the time of entry into force of this Convention for that State Party and any additional areas containing cluster munition remnants discovered after such entry into force;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p240 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(e)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">The total area containing cluster munition remnants cleared since entry into force of this Convention;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p240 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(f)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft58">The total area containing cluster munition remnants remaining to be cleared during the proposed extension;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p240 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(g)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The circumstances that have impeded the ability of the State Party to destroy all cluster munition remnants located in areas under its jurisdiction or control during the initial ten year period referred to in paragraph 1 of this Article, and those that may impede this ability during the proposed extension;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p240 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(h)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">The humanitarian, social, economic and environmental implications of the proposed extension; and</SPAN></P>
<P class="p240 ft16"><SPAN class="ft2">(i)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft60">Any other information relevant to the request for the proposed extension.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p225 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">7.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">The Meeting of States Parties or the Review Conference shall, taking into consideration the factors referred to in paragraph 6 of this Article, including, inter alia, the quantities of cluster munition remnants reported, assess the request and decide by a majority of votes of States Parties present and voting whether to grant the request for an extension. The States Parties may decide to grant a shorter extension than that requested and may propose benchmarks for the extension, as appropriate.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p224 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">8.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Such an extension may be renewed by a period of up to five years upon the submission of a new request, in accordance with paragraphs 5,</SPAN></P>
<P class="p218 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">6</SPAN><SPAN class="ft61">and 7 of this Article. In requesting a further extension a State Party shall submit relevant additional information on what has been undertaken during the previous extension granted pursuant to this Article.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p279 ft2">63</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_64">


<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t28">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr12 td56"><SPAN class="p280 ft2">Article 5</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr12 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr19 td56"><SPAN class="p280 ft30">Victim assistance</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr19 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Bilaga 1</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P class="p266 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">Each State Party with respect to cluster munition victims in areas under its jurisdiction or control shall, in accordance with applicable international humanitarian and human rights law, adequately provide ageand </SPAN><NOBR>gender-sensitive</NOBR> assistance, including medical care, rehabilitation and psychological support, as well as provide for their social and economic inclusion. Each State Party shall make every effort to collect reliable relevant data with respect to cluster munition victims.</P>
<P class="p281 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">In fulfilling its obligations under paragraph 1 of this Article each State Party shall:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p262 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Assess the needs of cluster munition victims;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">Develop, implement and enforce any necessary national laws andpolicies;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(c)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Develop a national plan and budget, including timeframes to carry out these activities, with a view to incorporating them within the existing national disability, development and human rights frameworks and mechanisms, while respecting the specific role and contribution of relevant actors;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p262 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(d)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Take steps to mobilise national and international resources;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(e)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Not discriminate against or among cluster munition victims, or between cluster munition victims and those who have suffered injuries or disabilities from other causes; differences in treatment should be based only on medical, rehabilitative, psychological or </SPAN><NOBR>socio-economic</NOBR> needs;</P>
<P class="p282 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(f)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft58">Closely consult with and actively involve cluster munition victims and their representative organisations;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(g)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Designate a focal point within the government for coordination of matters relating to the implementation of this Article; and</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(h)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">Strive to incorporate relevant guidelines and good practices including in the areas of medical care, rehabilitation and psychological support, as well as social and economic inclusion.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p283 ft2">Article 6</P>
<P class="p284 ft3">International cooperation and assistance</P>
<P class="p281 ft16"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft62">In fulfilling its obligations under this Convention each State Party has the right to seek and receive assistance.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p285 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">Each State Party in a position to do so shall provide technical, material and financial assistance to States Parties affected by cluster munitions, aimed at the implementation of the obligations of this Convention. Such assistance may be provided, inter alia, through the United Nations system, international, regional or national organisations or institutions, </SPAN><NOBR>non-governmental</NOBR> organisations or institutions, or on a bilateral basis.</P>
<P class="p286 ft2">64</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_65">


<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t27">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr12 td23"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">3.</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr12 td52"><SPAN class="p269 ft2">Each State Party undertakes to facilitate and shall have the right to</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr12 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD colspan=2 class="tr19 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">participate in the fullest possible exchange of equipment and scientific</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr19 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Bilaga 1</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P class="p287 ft4">and technological information concerning the implementation of this Convention. The States Parties shall not impose undue restrictions on the provision and receipt of clearance and other such equipment and related technological information for humanitarian purposes.</P>
<P class="p288 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">4.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">In addition to any obligations it may have pursuant to paragraph 4 of Article 4 of this Convention, each State Party in a position to do so shall provide assistance for clearance and destruction of cluster munition remnants and information concerning various means and technologies related to clearance of cluster munitions, as well as lists of experts, expert agencies or national points of contact on clearance and destruction of cluster munition remnants and related activities.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p288 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">5.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Each State Party in a position to do so shall provide assistance for the destruction of stockpiled cluster munitions, and shall also provide assistance to identify, assess and prioritise needs and practical measures in terms of marking, risk reduction education, protection of civilians and clearance and destruction as provided in Article 4 of this Convention.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p289 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">6.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Where, after entry into force of this Convention, cluster munitions have become cluster munition remnants located in areas under the jurisdiction or control of a State Party, each State Party in a position to do so shall urgently provide emergency assistance to the affected State Party.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p289 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">7.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">Each State Party in a position to do so shall provide assistance for the implementation of the obligations referred to in Article 5 of this Convention to adequately provide ageand </SPAN><NOBR>gender-sensitive</NOBR> assistance, including medical care, rehabilitation and psychological support, as well as provide for social and economic inclusion of cluster munition victims. Such assistance may be provided, inter alia, through the United Nations system, international, regional or national organisations or institutions, the International Committee of the Red Cross, national Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies and their International Federation, nongovernmental organisations or on a bilateral basis.</P>
<P class="p290 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">8.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Each State Party in a position to do so shall provide assistance to contribute to the economic and social recovery needed as a result of cluster munition use in affected States Parties.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p291 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">9.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Each State Party in a position to do so may contribute to relevant trust funds in order to facilitate the provision of assistance under this Article.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p291 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">10.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft55">Each State Party that seeks and receives assistance shall take all appropriate measures in order to facilitate the timely and effective implementation of this Convention, including facilitation of the entry and exit of personnel, materiel and equipment, in a manner consistent with</SPAN></P>
<P class="p292 ft2">65</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_66">


<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t29">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr12 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">national laws and regulations, taking into consideration international best</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr12 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr13 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">practices.</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr13 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Bilaga 1</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P class="p265 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">11.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft55">Each State Party may, with the purpose of developing a national action plan, request the United Nations system, regional organisations, other States Parties or other competent intergovernmental or nongovernmental institutions to assist its authorities to determine, inter alia:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The nature and extent of cluster munition remnants located in areas under its jurisdiction or control;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The financial, technological and human resources required for the implementation of the plan;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(c)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The time estimated as necessary to clear and destroy all cluster munition remnants located in areas under its jurisdiction or control;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(d)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">Risk reduction education programmes and awareness activities to reduce the incidence of injuries or deaths caused by cluster munition remnants;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p262 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(e)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Assistance to cluster munition victims; and</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(f)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft58">The coordination relationship between the government of the State Party concerned and the relevant governmental, intergovernmental or </SPAN><NOBR>non-governmental</NOBR> entities that will work in the implementation of the plan.</P>
<P class="p285 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">12.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft55">States Parties giving and receiving assistance under the provisions of this Article shall cooperate with a view to ensuring the full and prompt implementation of agreed assistance programmes.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p293 ft2">Article 7</P>
<P class="p294 ft3">Transparency measures</P>
<P class="p281 ft4">1. Each State Party shall report to the <NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations as soon as practicable, and in any event not later than 180 days after the entry into force of this Convention for that State Party, on:</P>
<P class="p263 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The national implementation measures referred to in Article 9 of this Convention;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The total of all cluster munitions, including explosive submunitions, referred to in paragraph 1 of Article 3 of this Convention, to include a breakdown of their type, quantity and, if possible, lot numbers of each type;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(c)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The technical characteristics of each type of cluster munition produced by that State Party prior to entry into force of this Convention for it, to the extent known, and those currently owned or possessed by it, giving, where reasonably possible, such categories of information as may facilitate identification and clearance of cluster munitions; at a minimum, this information shall include the dimensions, fusing, explosive content, metallic content, colour photographs and other information that may facilitate the clearance of cluster munition remnants;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p295 ft2">66</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_67">


<DIV>
<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p296 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(d)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">The status and progress of programmes for the conversion or decommissioning of production facilities for cluster munitions;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p296 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(e)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The status and progress of programmes for the destruction, in accordance with Article 3 of this Convention, of cluster munitions, including explosive submunitions, with details of the methods that will be used in destruction, the location of all destruction sites and the applicable safety and environmental standards to be observed;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p296 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(f)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft63">The types and quantities of cluster munitions, including explosive submunitions, destroyed in accordance with Article 3 of this Convention, including details of the methods of destruction used, the location of the destruction sites and the applicable safety and environmental standards observed;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p297 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(g)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft64">Stockpiles of cluster munitions, including explosive submunitions, discovered after reported completion of the programme referred to in </SPAN><NOBR>sub-paragraph</NOBR> (e) of this paragraph, and plans for their destruction in accordance with Article 3 of this Convention;</P>
<P class="p298 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(h)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft65">To the extent possible, the size and location of all cluster munition contaminated areas under its jurisdiction or control, to include as much detail as possible regarding the type and quantity of each type of cluster munition remnant in each such area and when they were used;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p296 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(i)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft59">The status and progress of programmes for the clearance and destruction of all types and quantities of cluster munition remnants cleared and destroyed in accordance with Article 4 of this Convention, to include the size and location of the cluster munition contaminated area cleared and a breakdown of the quantity of each type of cluster munition remnant cleared and destroyed;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p299 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(j)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft59">The measures taken to provide risk reduction education and, in particular, an immediate and effective warning to civilians living in cluster munition contaminated areas under its jurisdiction or control;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p300 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(k)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The status and progress of implementation of its obligations under Article 5 of this Convention to adequately provide ageand gendersensitive assistance, including medical care, rehabilitation and psychological support, as well as provide for social and economic inclusion of cluster munition victims and to collect reliable relevant data with respect to cluster munition victims;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p301 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(l)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft66">The name and contact details of the institutions mandated to provide information and to carry out the measures described in this paragraph;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p296 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(m)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft67">The amount of national resources, including financial, material or in kind, allocated to the implementation of Articles 3, 4 and 5 of this Convention; and</SPAN></P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p111 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</P>
<P class="p232 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p302 ft2">67</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_68">


<P class="p303 ft4">(n) The amounts, types and destinations of international Prop. 2011/12:47 cooperation and assistance provided under Article 6 of this Bilaga 1 Convention.</P>
<P class="p304 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">The information provided in accordance with paragraph 1 of this Article shall be updated by the States Parties annually, covering the previous calendar year, and reported to the </SPAN><NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations not later than 30 April of each year.</P>
<P class="p248 ft16"><SPAN class="ft2">3.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft62">The </SPAN><NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations shall transmit all such reports received to the States Parties.</P>
<P class="p305 ft2">Article 8</P>
<P class="p306 ft3">Facilitation and clarification of compliance</P>
<P class="p307 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">The States Parties agree to consult and cooperate with each other regarding the implementation of the provisions of this Convention and to work together in a spirit of cooperation to facilitate compliance by States Parties with their obligations under this Convention.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p248 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">If one or more States Parties wish to clarify and seek to resolve questions relating to a matter of compliance with the provisions of this Convention by another State Party, it may submit, through the Secretary- General of the United Nations, a Request for Clarification of that matter to that State Party. Such a request shall be accompanied by all appropriate information. Each State Party shall refrain from unfounded Requests for Clarification, care being taken to avoid abuse. A State Party that receives a Request for Clarification shall provide, through the </SPAN><NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations, within 28 days to the requesting State Party all information that would assist in clarifying the matter.</P>
<P class="p308 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">3.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">If the requesting State Party does not receive a response through the Secretary- General of the United Nations within that time period, or deems the response to the Request for Clarification to be unsatisfactory, it may submit the matter through the </SPAN><NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations to the next Meeting of States Parties. The <NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations shall transmit the submission, accompanied by all appropriate information pertaining to the Request for Clarification, to all States Parties. All such information shall be presented to the requested State Party which shall have the right to respond.</P>
<P class="p309 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">4.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Pending the convening of any Meeting of States Parties, any of the States Parties concerned may request the </SPAN><NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations to exercise his or her good offices to facilitate the clarification requested.</P>
<P class="p310 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">5.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Where a matter has been submitted to it pursuant to paragraph 3 of this Article, the Meeting of States Parties shall first determine whether to consider that matter further, taking into account all information submitted by the States Parties concerned. If it does so determine, the</SPAN></P>
<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t21">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr13 td51"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Meeting of States Parties may suggest to the States Parties concerned</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr13 td44"><SPAN class="p15 ft2">68</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_69">


<P class="p311 ft4">ways and means further to clarify or resolve the matter under Prop. 2011/12:47 consideration, including the initiation of appropriate procedures in Bilaga 1 conformity with international law. In circumstances where the issue at</P>
<P class="p206 ft4">hand is determined to be due to circumstances beyond the control of the requested State Party, the Meeting of States Parties may recommend appropriate measures, including the use of cooperative measures referred to in Article 6 of this Convention.</P>
<P class="p312 ft2">6. In addition to the procedures provided for in paragraphs 2 to 5 of this Article, the Meeting of States Parties may decide to adopt such other general procedures or specific mechanisms for clarification of compliance, including facts, and resolution of instances of noncompliance with the provisions of this Convention as it deems appropriate.</P>
<P class="p313 ft2">Article 9</P>
<P class="p314 ft3">National implementation measures</P>
<P class="p258 ft4">Each State Party shall take all appropriate legal, administrative and other measures to implement this Convention, including the imposition of penal sanctions to prevent and suppress any activity prohibited to a State Party under this Convention undertaken by persons or on territory under its jurisdiction or control.</P>
<P class="p315 ft2">Article 10</P>
<P class="p316 ft3">Settlement of disputes</P>
<P class="p317 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">When a dispute arises between two or more States Parties relating to the interpretation or application of this Convention, the States Parties concerned shall consult together with a view to the expeditious settlement of the dispute by negotiation or by other peaceful means of their choice, including recourse to the Meeting of States Parties and referral to the International Court of Justice in conformity with the Statute of the Court.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p318 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">The Meeting of States Parties may contribute to the settlement of the dispute by whatever means it deems appropriate, including offering its good offices, calling upon the States Parties concerned to start the settlement procedure of their choice and recommending a </SPAN><NOBR>time-limit</NOBR> for any agreed procedure.</P>
<P class="p319 ft2">Article 11</P>
<P class="p320 ft3">Meetings of States Parties</P>
<P class="p258 ft4">1. The States Parties shall meet regularly in order to consider and, where necessary, take decisions in respect of any matter with regard to the application or implementation of this Convention, including:</P>
<P class="p275 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">The operation and status of this Convention;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p272 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Matters arising from the reports submitted under the provisions of this Convention;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p275 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(c)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">International cooperation and assistance in accordance with</SPAN></P>
<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t30">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr16 td57"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Article 6 of this Convention;</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr16 td58"><SPAN class="p15 ft2">69</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_70">


<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t31">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr12 td59"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">(d) The development of technologies to clear cluster munition</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr12 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr19 td59"><SPAN class="p321 ft2">remnants;</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr19 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Bilaga 1</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P class="p263 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(e)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">Submissions of States Parties under Articles 8 and 10 of this Convention; and</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft16"><SPAN class="ft2">(f)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft68">Submissions of States Parties as provided for in Articles 3 and 4 of this Convention.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p265 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">The first Meeting of States Parties shall be convened by the </SPAN><NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations within one year of entry into force of this Convention. The subsequent meetings shall be convened by the <NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations annually until the first Review Conference.</P>
<P class="p285 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">3.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">States not party to this Convention, as well as the United Nations, other relevant international organisations or institutions, regional organisations, the International Committee of the Red Cross, the International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies and relevant </SPAN><NOBR>non-governmental</NOBR> organisations may be invited to attend these meetings as observers in accordance with the agreed rules of procedure.</P>
<P class="p322 ft2">Article 12</P>
<P class="p323 ft3">Review Conferences</P>
<P class="p281 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">A Review Conference shall be convened by the </SPAN><NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations five years after the entry into force of this Convention. Further Review Conferences shall be convened by the <NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations if so requested by one or more States Parties, provided that the interval between Review Conferences shall in no case be less than five years. All States Parties to this Convention shall be invited to each Review Conference.</P>
<P class="p324 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">The purpose of the Review Conference shall be:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p325 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">To review the operation and status of this Convention;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">To consider the need for and the interval between further Meetings of States Parties referred to in paragraph 2 of Article 11 of this Convention; and</SPAN></P>
<P class="p263 ft16"><SPAN class="ft2">(c)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft48">To take decisions on submissions of States Parties as provided for in Articles 3 and 4 of this Convention.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p326 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">3.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">States not party to this Convention, as well as the United Nations, other relevant international organisations or institutions, regional organisations, the International Committee of the Red Cross, the International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies and relevant </SPAN><NOBR>non-governmental</NOBR> organisations may be invited to attend each Review Conference as observers in accordance with the agreed rules of procedure.</P>
<P class="p327 ft2">70</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_71">


<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t32">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr12 td60"><SPAN class="p328 ft2">Article 13</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr12 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr13 td60"><SPAN class="p328 ft3">Amendments</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr13 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Bilaga 1</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P class="p254 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">At any time after its entry into force any State Party may propose amendments to this Convention. Any proposal for an amendment shall be communicated to the </SPAN><NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations, who shall circulate it to all States Parties and shall seek their views on whether an Amendment Conference should be convened to consider the proposal. If a majority of the States Parties notify the <NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations no later than 90 days after its circulation that they support further consideration of the proposal, the <NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations shall convene an Amendment Conference to which all States Parties shall be invited.</P>
<P class="p329 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">States not party to this Convention, as well as the United Nations, other relevant international organisations or institutions, regional organisations, the International Committee of the Red Cross, the International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies and relevant </SPAN><NOBR>non-governmental</NOBR> organisations may be invited to attend each Amendment Conference as observers in accordance with the agreed rules of procedure.</P>
<P class="p318 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">3.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">The Amendment Conference shall be held immediately following a Meeting of States Parties or a Review Conference unless a majority of the States Parties request that it be held earlier.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p255 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">4.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Any amendment to this Convention shall be adopted by a majority of twothirds of the States Parties present and voting at the Amendment Conference. The Depositary shall communicate any amendment so adopted to all States.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p254 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">5.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">An amendment to this Convention shall enter into force for States Parties that have accepted the amendment on the date of deposit of acceptances by a majority of the States which were Parties at the date of adoption of the amendment. Thereafter it shall enter into force for any remaining State Party on the date of deposit of its instrument of acceptance.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p315 ft2">Article 14</P>
<P class="p330 ft3">Costs and administrative tasks</P>
<P class="p258 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">The costs of the Meetings of States Parties, the Review Conferences and the Amendment Conferences shall be borne by the States Parties and States not party to this Convention participating therein, in accordance with the United Nations scale of assessment adjusted appropriately.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p258 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">The costs incurred by the </SPAN><NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations under Articles 7 and 8 of this Convention shall be borne by the States Parties in accordance with the United Nations scale of assessment</P>
<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t21">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr13 td61"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">adjusted appropriately.</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr13 td62"><SPAN class="p15 ft2">71</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_72">


<TABLE cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 class="t29">
<TR>
	<TD class="tr12 td23"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">3.</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr12 td52"><SPAN class="p269 ft2">The performance by the <NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations</SPAN> </TD>

</TR>

<P class="p331 ft2">subject to an appropriate United Nations mandate.</P>
<P class="p332 ft2">Article 15</P>
<P class="p333 ft3">Signature</P>
<P class="p334 ft16">This Convention, done at Dublin on 30 May 2008, shall be open for signature at Oslo by all States on 3 December 2008 and thereafter at United Nations Headquarters in New York until its entry into force.</P>
<P class="p335 ft2">Article 16</P>
<P class="p336 ft3">Ratification, acceptance, approval or accession</P>
<P class="p281 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">This Convention is subject to ratification, acceptance or approval by the Signatories.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p337 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">It shall be open for accession by any State that has not signed the Convention.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p337 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">3.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">The instruments of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession shall be deposited with the Depositary.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p338 ft2">Article 17</P>
<P class="p339 ft3">Entry into force</P>
<P class="p281 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">This Convention shall enter into force on the first day of the sixth month after the month in which the thirtieth instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession has been deposited.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p340 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">For any State that deposits its instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession after the date of the deposit of the thirtieth instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession, this Convention shall enter into force on the first day of the sixth month after the date on which that State has deposited its instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p341 ft2">Article 18</P>
<P class="p342 ft3">Provisional application</P>
<P class="p281 ft4">Any State may, at the time of its ratification, acceptance, approval or accession, declare that it will apply provisionally Article 1 of this Convention pending its entry into force for that State.</P>
<P class="p338 ft2">Article 19</P>
<P class="p343 ft3">Reservations</P>
<P class="p344 ft2">The Articles of this Convention shall not be subject to reservations.</P>
<P class="p345 ft2">72</P>

</TR>
</TABLE>
<P class="p347 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">This Convention shall be of unlimited duration.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p221 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Each State Party shall, in exercising its national sovereignty, have the right to withdraw from this Convention. It shall give notice of such withdrawal to all other States Parties, to the Depositary and to the United Nations Security Council. Such instrument of withdrawal shall include a full explanation of the reasons motivating withdrawal.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p222 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">3.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">Such withdrawal shall only take effect six months after the receipt of the instrument of withdrawal by the Depositary. If, however, on the expiry of that sixmonth period, the withdrawing State Party is engaged in an armed conflict, the withdrawal shall not take effect before the end of the armed conflict.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p348 ft2">Article 21</P>
<P class="p349 ft3">Relations with States not party to this Convention</P>
<P class="p221 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Each State Party shall encourage States not party to this Convention to ratify, accept, approve or accede to this Convention, with the goal of attracting the adherence of all States to this Convention.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p223 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Each State Party shall notify the governments of all States not party to this Convention, referred to in paragraph 3 of this Article, of its obligations under this Convention, shall promote the norms it establishes and shall make its best efforts to discourage States not party to this Convention from using cluster munitions.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p222 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">3.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft49">Notwithstanding the provisions of Article 1 of this Convention and in accordance with international law, States Parties, their military personnel or nationals, may engage in military cooperation and operations with States not party to this Convention that might engage in activities prohibited to a State Party.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p347 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">4.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft57">Nothing in paragraph 3 of this Article shall authorise a State</SPAN></P>
<P class="p350 ft2">Party:</P>
<P class="p351 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">To develop, produce or otherwise acquire cluster munitions;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p239 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">To itself stockpile or transfer cluster munitions;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p239 ft2"><SPAN class="ft2">(c)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft46">To itself use cluster munitions; or</SPAN></P>
<P class="p352 ft4"><SPAN class="ft2">(d)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft47">To expressly request the use of cluster munitions in cases where the choice of munitions used is within its exclusive control.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p353 ft2">Article 22</P>
<P class="p242 ft3">Depositary</P>
<P class="p354 ft4">The <NOBR>Secretary-General</NOBR> of the United Nations is hereby designated as the Depositary of this Convention.</P>
<P class="p72 ft2">73</P>
</DIV>

	<TD class="tr12 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>

	<TD class="tr28 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>

	<TD class="tr13 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Convention shall be equally authentic.</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr13 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>

<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p122 ft3">Inofficiell svensk översättning</P>
<P class="p357 ft37">DIPLOMATISK KONFERENS FÖR ANTAGANDET AV EN KONVENTION OM KLUSTERAMMUNITION</P>
<P class="p358 ft18">DUBLIN, <NOBR>19–30</NOBR> MAJ 2008</P>
<P class="p359 ft18">Konvention om klusterammunition</P>
<P class="p360 ft2">Statsparterna i denna konvention,</P>
<P class="p357 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">som är djupt oroade över </SPAN>att det fortfarande är civilbefolkningen och enskilda civilpersoner som drabbas hårdast vid väpnade konflikter,</P>
<P class="p361 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">som är beslutna </SPAN>att en gång för alla göra slut på det lidande och de förluster som orsakas av klusterammunition då de används, när de inte fungerar som avsett eller när de har övergetts,</P>
<P class="p362 ft2"><SPAN class="ft3">som är oroade över </SPAN>att lämningar av klusterammunition dödar och lemlästar civilpersoner, däribland kvinnor och barn, hindrar ekonomisk och social utveckling, bland annat genom förlusten av utkomstmöjligheter, försvårar rehabilitering och återuppbyggnad efter konflikter, fördröjer eller förhindrar flyktingars och internflyktingars återvändande, kan inverka negativt på nationella och internationella insatser för fredsbyggande och humanitärt bistånd samt har andra allvarliga konsekvenser som kan bestå i många år efter användningen,</P>
<P class="p363 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">som även är djupt oroade över </SPAN>den fara som de stora nationella lagren av klusterammunition som bibehålls för operativ användning utgör och som är fast beslutna att se till att dessa snabbt förstörs,</P>
<P class="p362 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">som anser </SPAN>det vara nödvändigt att på ett verkningsfullt och samordnat sätt effektivt bidra till att ta itu med utmaningen att röja lämningar av klusterammunition över hela världen och se till att de förstörs,</P>
<P class="p362 ft16"><SPAN class="ft15">som även är beslutna </SPAN>att se till att de rättigheter som tillkommer alla klusterammunitionsoffer förverkligas fullt ut och som erkänner deras inneboende värde,</P>
<P class="p133 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">som har föresatt sig </SPAN>att göra sitt yttersta för att tillhandahålla stöd till klusterammunitionsoffer, inbegripet sjukvård, rehabilitering och psykologiskt stöd, och sörja för deras sociala och ekonomiska integrering,</P>
<P class="p362 ft16"><SPAN class="ft15">som inser </SPAN>behovet av att tillhandahålla ålders- och könsanpassat stöd till klusterammunitionsoffer och tillgodose sårbara gruppers särskilda behov,</P>
<P class="p364 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">som beaktar </SPAN>konventionen om rättigheter för personer med funktionsnedsättning, enligt vilken statsparterna i den konventionen bland annat åtar sig att säkerställa och främja fullt förverkligande av alla mänskliga rättigheter och grundläggande friheter för alla personer med</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p122 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</P>
<P class="p183 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p302 ft2">75</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_76">


<DIV>
<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p19 ft16">funktionsnedsättning utan diskriminering av något slag på grund av funktionsnedsättning,</P>
<P class="p228 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">som är uppmärksamma </SPAN>på behovet av att i lämplig grad samordna insatser som görs i olika fora för att tillgodose rättigheterna för och behoven hos dem som drabbats av olika typer av vapen och som har föresatt sig att förhindra att åtskillnad görs mellan dem som drabbats av olika typer av vapen,</P>
<P class="p228 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">som bekräftar </SPAN>att civilpersoner och kombattanter, i de fall denna konvention eller andra internationella överenskommelser inte är tillämpliga, ska stå under de folkrättsliga principers skydd och överhöghet, som härleder sig från etablerad sedvana, humanitetens principer och det allmänna samvetets bud.</P>
<P class="p228 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">som även är beslutna </SPAN>att väpnade grupper som skiljer sig från en stats väpnade styrkor inte under några omständigheter ska tillåtas ägna sig åt verksamhet som är förbjuden för en statspart i denna konvention,</P>
<P class="p229 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">som välkomnar </SPAN>det mycket breda internationella stödet för den internationella norm som förbjuder antipersonella minor, inskriven i 1997 års konvention om förbud mot användning, lagring, produktion och överföring av antipersonella minor (truppminor) samt om deras förstöring,</P>
<P class="p365 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">som även välkomnar </SPAN>antagandet av protokollet om explosiva lämningar efter krig, som är fogat till konventionen om förbud mot eller inskränkningar i användningen av vissa konventionella vapen som kan anses vara ytterst skadebringande eller ha urskillningslösa verkningar, och dess ikraftträdande den 12 november 2006 och som önskar förbättra civilpersoners skydd mot verkningarna av lämningar av klusterammunition i områden där konflikter har ägt rum,</P>
<P class="p231 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">som även beaktar </SPAN>Förenta nationernas säkerhetsråds resolution 1325 om kvinnor, fred och säkerhet och Förenta nationernas säkerhetsråds resolution 1612 om barn och väpnade konflikter,</P>
<P class="p229 ft4"><SPAN class="ft20">som vidare välkomnar </SPAN>de åtgärder som under senare år vidtagits nationellt, regionalt och globalt i syfte att förbjuda, begränsa eller avbryta användning, lagring, tillverkning och överföring av klusterammunition,</P>
<P class="p366 ft2"><SPAN class="ft3">som betonar </SPAN>det allmänna medvetandets betydelse för att främja principerna om humanitet, en betydelse som framgår av det världsomspännande kravet på ett slut på av klusterammunition orsakat civilt lidande, och som erkänner de insatser på detta område som gjorts av Förenta nationerna, Internationella rödakorskommittén, Koalitionen mot klusterammunition och många andra enskilda organisationer i hela världen,</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p111 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</P>
<P class="p232 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p233 ft2">76</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_77">

	<TD class="tr12 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2"><SPAN class="ft3">som bekräftar </SPAN>förklaringen från Oslokonferensen om klusterammunition,</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr12 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">Prop. 2011/12:47</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>

	<TD class="tr19 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">där staterna bland annat erkände de allvarliga konsekvenser som</SPAN> </TD>

</TR>

	<TD class="tr20 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">användningen av klusterammunition har orsakat och förband sig att</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>

	<TD class="tr20 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">senast 2008 sluta ett rättsligt bindande avtal vilket förbjuder användning,</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>

	<TD class="tr19 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">tillverkning, överföring och lagring av klusterammunition som orsakar</SPAN> </TD>

	<TD class="tr20 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">oacceptabel skada på civilpersoner, och som upprättar en ram för</SPAN> </TD>

</TR>

	<TD class="tr21 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">samt förstöring av lager,</SPAN> </TD>

</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr22 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2"><SPAN class="ft3">som betonar </SPAN>det önskvärda i att få alla stater att ansluta sig till denna</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr22 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr20 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">konvention och som är beslutna att arbeta ihärdigt för att den ska bli</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr21 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">allmängiltig och genomföras fullständigt,</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr21 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr22 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2"><SPAN class="ft3">som stöder sig </SPAN>på den internationella humanitära rättens principer och</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr22 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr20 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">regler, i synnerhet principen att parterna i en väpnad konflikt inte har</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr19 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">obegränsad rätt att välja stridsmetoder och stridsmedel samt reglerna att</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr19 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr20 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">parterna i en konflikt alltid ska göra åtskillnad mellan civilbefolkningen</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr20 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">och kombattanter och mellan civil egendom och militära mål och</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr19 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">följaktligen ska rikta sina operationer enbart mot militära mål, att</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr19 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr20 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">försiktighet ständigt ska iakttas vid genomförandet av militära</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr20 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">operationer för att skydda civilbefolkningen, civilpersoner och civil</SPAN> </TD>
	<TD class="tr20 td53"><SPAN class="p14 ft8">&nbsp;</SPAN> </TD>
</TR>
<TR>
	<TD class="tr19 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">egendom och att civilbefolkningen och enskilda civilpersoner åtnjuter</SPAN> </TD>

	<TD class="tr21 td54"><SPAN class="p14 ft2">allmänt skydd mot faror som härrör från militära operationer,</SPAN> </TD>
